Eggeling
  1. Now, they slay the sacrifice, when they spread (perform) it:–to wit, when they press out the king (Soma), they slay him; when they quiet the victim, they slay it; and with mortar and pestle, with the upper and nether millstone, they slay the havis offering.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

[рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рдердореЗ]

Eggeling
  1. When slain, that sacrifice was no longer vigorous. By means of dakshiс╣З─Бs (gifts to the priests) the gods invigorated it: hence the name dakshiс╣З─Б, because thereby they invigorated (dakshay) it. Whatever, therefore, fails in this sacrifice, when slain, that he now invigorates by means of gifts to the priests; then the sacrifice becomes indeed successful: for this reason he makes gifts to the priests.

Eggeling
  1. Now at the Haviryaj├▒a, indeed, they give as little as six or twelve (cows 3), but no Soma-sacrifice should have dakshiс╣З─Бs of less than a hundred. For

he, Praj─Бpati 4, forsooth, is the visible sacrifice; and man is nearest to Praj─Бpati, and he has a life of a hundred years, a hundred powers, a hundred energies. Only by a hundred he invigorates him, and not by less than a hundred: wherefore no Soma-sacrifice should have dakshiс╣З─Бs of less than a hundred; nor should any one officiate as a priest for a sacrificer at a (Soma-sacrifice) where less than a hundred are given,–’lest he should be an eyewitness when they will but slay and not invigorate him (Soma).’

рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗрдг рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рддрд┐- рджреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рд╡реИ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ ред ‘рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ’ ‘рджреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рд╡реИ’ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдГ ред “рдкреНрд░рдердордЪрд░рдорддрдпрд╛реж”- рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рез ред рез ред рейрей) рдЬрд╕рд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдирд╛рдорд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкреЗрди рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдирд╛рддреНрддрджрднрд╛рд╡рдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рджреНрд╡реИрд╡рд┐рдзреНрдпрдореЗрд╡ рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ- рдЕрд╣реИрд╡ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ’ ‘рдЕрд╣реЗрд╡’ рд╕реНрд╡рдд рдПрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдпреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ рдПрдХрд╡рд┐рдзрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ ред ‘рдЕрде рдпреЗ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдГ’ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╛рдГ ‘рдЕрдиреВрдЪрд╛рдирд╛рдГ’ рд╕рд╛рдЩреНрдЧреЗ рд╡реЗрджреЗ рдЕрдзреАрддрд┐рдирдГ ред тАЬрдЙрдкреЗрдпрд┐рд╡рд╛рдирдирд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирдиреВрдЪрд╛рдирд╢реНрдЪ” (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рей ред реи ред резрежреп) рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрдиреВрдЪрд╛рдирд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрд┐рддрдГ ред ‘рд╢реБрд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ’ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рдиреНрддрдГ ред “рдХреНрд╡рд╕реБрд╢реНрдЪ”- (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рей ред реи ред резрежрен) рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреНрд╡рд╕реБрдГ ред ‘рддреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рджрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред ‘рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рджреНрд╡реЗрдзрд╛ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рддреБ рдирд┐рдЧрджрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрдореН рее рек рее

Eggeling
  1. Now, truly, there are two kinds of gods; for the gods, forsooth, are the gods; and the learned Br─Бhmans versed in sacred lore are the human gods. And the sacrifice to them is twofold, oblations (being the sacrifice) to the gods, and gifts to the priests being that to the human gods, to the learned Br─Бhmans versed in sacred lore. With oblations, forsooth, one gratifies the gods, and with gifts to the priests the human gods, the learned Br─Бhmans versed in sacred lore. These two kinds of gods, when gratified, convey him to the heavenly world.

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

Eggeling
  1. But it is to the officiating priests, forsooth, that these gifts of his belong, for they prepare him another self,–to wit, this sacrifice, consisting of R╠еc and Yajus and S─Бman and oblations,–that becomes his self in yonder world: ‘It is they that have generated me,’ from this (consideration) he should give the gifts to officiating priests and not to non-officiating.

Eggeling
  1. Having gone back to the G─Бrhapatya fire 6, he

offers the gift offerings. Having tied a piece of gold in a fringed cloth 7, and laid it (into the spoon), he offers. ‘May there be a place for me in the world of the gods!’ With this hope he offers whoever offers: that same sacrifice of his goes to the world of the gods; and behind it goes the gift he gives to the priests, and holding on to the gift follows the sacrificer.

Eggeling
  1. Now, there are four (kinds of) gifts to priests,–gold, the cow, cloth, and the horse. But it is not proper that he should lay a horse’s foot or a cow’s foot (into the spoon): hence he ties up a piece of gold in a fringed cloth, and having laid it (into the spoon) he offers.

  1. He offers with two verses to the Sun. For yonder world is shut off by darkness; and dispelling the darkness by that light he reaches the heavenly world: therefore he offers with two verses to the Sun.

Eggeling
  1. He offers with this g─Бyatr─л verse (V─Бj. S. VII, 41; Rig-veda I, 50, 1), ‘The lights bear on high that divine knower of beings, S┼лrya, that all may see him,–Hail!’–for the g─Бyatr─л is this earth, and she is a safe resting-place hence he thereby stands firmly on this safe resting-place.

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

рдЕрде рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рдВ рдЬреБрд╣реЛрддрд┐- “рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореБрджрдЧрд╛рджрдиреАрдХрдВ ред рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрд░реНрдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ ред рдЖрдкреНрд░рд╛ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рд╜рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдЬрдЧрддрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдереБрд╖рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛тАЭ- (рд╡рд╛. рд╕рдВ. рен ред рекреи) рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрддрдпрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрд╛ рд▓реЛрдХрдореЗрд╡реИрддрдпреЛрдкрдкреНрд░реИрддрд┐ рее резреж рее

Eggeling
  1. He then makes the second offering with this trishс╣нubh verse (V─Бj. S. VII, 42; Rig-veda I, 115, I), ‘The brilliant front 10 of the gods hath risen,

the eye of Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and Agni: S┼лrya, the soul of the movable and immovable, hath filled the heaven and the earth and the air,–Hail!’ whereby he approaches the world (of the gods).

‘рджрджрд╛рддрд┐’ рее резрез рее

Eggeling
  1. He then makes either one or two oblations on the ─Аgn─лdhra (fire). The reason why he makes one or two oblations on the ─Аgn─лdhra fire is that Agni rules over beasts (cattle) 11, and they lie round about him on every side: it is him he pleases by this oblation, and thus pleased he is gracious unto this (sacrificer), and the latter offers (to the priests a cow) graciously given up by him (Agni).

Eggeling
  1. He offers with (V─Бj. S. VII, 43; Rig-veda I, 189, 1), ‘O Agni, lead us on a good path unto wealth; thou, O god, that knowest all works! keep thou from us the sin that leadeth astray, and we will offer unto thee most ample adoration,–‘Hail!’ Thereupon, if he intends to give away a horse, harnessed or unharnessed, let him make a second oblation; but if not, he need not attend to this.

рд╕ рдЬреБрд╣реЛрддрд┐- “рдЕрдпрдВ рдиреЛ рд╜рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд░рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдХреГрдгреЛрддреНрд╡рдпрдВ рдореГрдзрдГ рдкреБрд░ рдПрддреБ рдкреНрд░рднрд┐рдиреНрджрдиреН ред рдЕрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдЮреНрдЬрдпрддреБ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддрд╛рд╡рдпрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдЮреНрдЬрдпрддреБ рдЬрд░реНрд╣реГрд╖рд╛рдгрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛”- (рд╡рд╛. рд╕рдВ. рен ред рекрек) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛ рд╣реНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рдГ рее резрей рее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рд╣реБрддреЗрдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдорд╛рд╣- рд╕ рдЬреБрд╣реЛрддреНрдпрдпрдВ рдиреЛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ 12 ред рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдХрд░рдгрдпреЛрдГ”- (рдзрд╛. рдкрд╛. рднреНрд╡рд╛. рдк. репрек) “рд╡рд┐рдиреНрд╡рд┐рдХреГрдгреНрд╡реНрдпреЛрд░ рдЪтАЭ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рей ред рез ред реореж) рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдордпрдВ рдзрдирдореЗрд╡ рдХрд░реЛрддреБ рдХрд┐рдиреНрддреБ ‘рдореГрдзрдГ’ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛рдиреН ‘рдкреНрд░рднрд┐рдиреНрджрдиреН’ рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рджреН ‘рдПрддреБ’ рдмреГрд╣рджреНрд╡рдпрдГ” (рддреИ. рд╢рд╛. рей ред реп ред рел) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рдп рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрдирдирд╛рдордзрдпреЗрдореН (рдирд┐рдШрдВ. реи ред рен ред рен) рдпрддреЛ рд╜рд╢реНрд╡реЛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее резрей рее

Eggeling
  1. He offers with (V─Бj. S. VII, 44), ‘May this Agni make wide room for us: may he march in front smiting the haters! May he gain riches in the winning of riches: may he, fiercely rushing, conquer the enemies! Hail!’ for the horse is a winner of riches (spoils, prizes).

резрек

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ

(рд╢реНрд╡реЛс│Ш рд╜рде) рдЕс│Шрде рд╣рд┐с│Шрд░рдгреНрдпрдорд╛рджрд╛с│Шрдп рд╢рд╛с│Шрд▓рд╛рдорднреНрдпреИс│Шрддрд┐рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╢реНрд░реАрдзрд░рд╛рджрд┐

(рд╢реНрд╡реЛс│Ш рд╜рде) рдЕс│Шрде рд╣рд┐с│Шрд░рдгреНрдпрдорд╛рджрд╛с│Шрдп рд╢рд╛с│Шрд▓рд╛рдорднреНрдпреИс│Шрддрд┐рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН - Weber

рдЕс│Шрде рд╣рд┐с│Шрд░рдгреНрдпрдорд╛рджрд╛с│Шрдп рд╢рд╛с│Шрд▓рд╛рдорднреНрдпреИс│Шрддрд┐рее

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon, taking some gold, (the sacrificer)

goes to the hall. South of the altar stand the Dakshiс╣З─Б (cows). Standing in front of the hall, he respectfully addresses them 14 with (V─Бj. S. VII, 45), ‘By your beauty have I come to beauty.’ Now at first cattle did not submit to being given away. Laying aside their own beauteous forms 15 they approached with their (bare) bodies. The gods then went up to them from the offering ground with their (the animalsтАЩ) own forms; and they, knowing their own forms, resigned themselves and became well-disposed to being given away. And in like manner does he now go up to them from the offering ground with their own forms; and they, knowing their own forms, resign themselves and become well-disposed to being given away.

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

Eggeling
  1. ‘May the all-knowing Tutha distribute you!’–Now, Tutha is the Brahman: he thus distributes them by means of the Brahman. And the Brahman knows who is fit to receive a dakshiс╣З─Б and who is unfit: thus these (cows) of his are given away only to him who is fit to receive a dakshiс╣З─Б and not to him who is unfit.

Eggeling
  1. ‘Go ye forward in the way of truth,’–for whosoever walks in the way of the gods, walks in the way of truth;–‘ye of shining (candra) gifts!’ whereby they walk with that light (candra, the moon).

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he looks on the Sadas, with, ‘Unite with the Sadas-priests!’ whereby he means to say, ‘May the Sadas-priests not go beyond thee!’

Eggeling
  1. He then takes the gold and goes up to the ─Аgn─лdhra (fire-house), saying (V─Бj. S. VII, 46), ‘May I this day obtain a Br─Бhman who has a father and forefathers!’–for he who is renowned and of renowned family, is one who has a father and forefathers; and by the gifts which he gives to a renowned (priest), though they be but few, he gains great things.–‘A R╠еshi, the scion of R╠еshis,’ for he who is renowned as learned in sacred lore, is a R╠еshi, the scion of R╠еshis;–‘of well-bestowed gifts,’ for he indeed is one on whom gifts are well-bestowed.

Eggeling
  1. Having thus respectfully sat down by the Agn─лdh, he gives him the gold, with ‘Given (r─Бta) by us, go ye to the gods!’–for whatever sacrificial gift he gives unhesitatingly, with a liberal (r─Бta) mind, thereby he gains great things, ‘Go ye to the gods,’ he says, for he who sacrifices, sacrifices with the hope, ‘May there be a place for me in the world of the gods;’ and he thus makes him a sharer in the world of the gods.–‘Enter ye to the Giver!’ whereby he means to say, ‘Enter ye into me!’ and thus those (cows) 18 do not get lost to him. And as to his giving

a dakshiс╣З─Б first to the Agn─лdh, it was from thence (from the ─Аgn─лdhra) 19 that all the gods gained immortality: therefore he gives the dakshiс╣З─Б first to the Agn─лdh.

Eggeling
  1. Then, approaching in the same way, he gives some gold to an ─Аtreya 21. For, at the time 22 when they recite the morning prayer, they were once upon a time singing praises here in front 23. Now Atri was the Hotr╠е of the R╠еshis. Then the darkness of the Asuras came rushing into the Sadas. The R╠еshis said to Atri, ‘Come back here, and dispel this darkness!’ He dispelled that darkness; and thinking, ‘He indeed is the light who has dispelled this darkness,’ they brought him this light, gold, for a sacrificial gift,–for gold is indeed light; and by that same splendour and energy the R╠еshi dispelled the darkness. And so does he now also dispel the darkness by that light: therefore he bestows gold on an ─Аtreya.

рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╢реНрд░реАрдзрд░рд╛рджрд┐

(рддреНрдпс│Ш) рдЕс│Шрде рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдос│ШрдгреЗрее

Eggeling
  1. Then to the Brahman, for the Brahman watches over the sacrifice from the south. Then to the Udg─Бtr╠е (chanter); then to the Hotr╠е; then to the two Adhvaryus, seated in the cart-shed. Then, having returned (to the Sadas he presents gold) to the Prastotr╠е; then to the Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa; then to the Br─Бhmaс╣З─Бchaс╣Бsin; then to the Potr╠е; then to the Neshс╣нr╠е; then to the Ach─Бv─Бka; then to the Unnetr╠е; then to the Gr─Бvastut; then to the Subrahmaс╣Зy─Б. To the Pratihartr╠е he presents it last, since he is the restrainer(pratihartr╠е) 26: he thus in the end restrains (the cows) for him, and so they do not become lost to him.

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he (the Adhvaryu) says (to the Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa), ‘Recite (the invitatory prayer) to Indra, followed by the Maruts!’ Now when, in the beginning, Praj─Бpati gave gifts, Indra thought within himself, ‘Everything here, forsooth, he will give away, and not anything will he leave for us.’ He then, to stop the giving, raised up that thunderbolt ‘Recite to Indra Marutvat!’ and thereafter he (Praj─Бpati) gave no more. And in like manner is that thunderbolt ‘Recite to Indra Marutvat!’ now raised up to stop the giving, and thereafter he (the sacrificer) gives no more.

Eggeling
  1. And whatever other gift he gives that he gives with the hope, ‘May I also have this in yonder world!’ That he accepts with (V─Бj. S. VII, 48), ‘Who hath given it? to whom hath he given it? Hope hath given it, for Hope hath he given it: Hope is the giver, Hope the receiver. This to thee, O Hope!’ Thus he assigns it to a deity.

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдирд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее рек-рей-рек рее

Eggeling
  1. Here they say 32,–Let him not assign it to any deity; for whatsoever deity he here kindles, that deity, being kindled, becomes ever more glorious from one day to the morrow; and to whatever fire he here adds fuel, that fire, being kindled, becomes ever more glorious from one day to the morrow; and ever more glorious does he become, whosoever, knowing this, accepts (a gift): even as one offers in kindled fire, so does he offer that (gift) which he gives to one learned in the scriptures. Therefore he who is learned in the scriptures need not assign (the gift to a deity).
Eggeling

24; There are, then, four (kinds of) sacrificial gifts: Gold–thereby indeed he preserves his own life, for gold is life. That he (Praj─Бpati or Varuс╣Зa) gave

to Agni, performing the office of the Agn─лdh (fire-kindler): wherefore now also gold is given to the Agn─лdh.

  32. 349:1 The K─Бс╣Зva text of this paragraph seems more correct: Thus he assigns it to deities; for when he bestows (abhy─Бdh─Б) anything on a deity, that deity thereby shines ever more brilliantly; and whatever (fuel) he adds to the fire, thereby it shines ever more brilliantly: and more glorious does he become from day to day whosoever, knowing it, accepts it thus. Here now ─Аsuri said, ‘But he who is learned in the scriptures need not regard this; for as one puts fuel on kindled fire, and offers on kindled fire, thus he gives who gives gifts to one learned in the scriptures.’ ↩︎
